b4:["$","ul",null,{"children":["\n",["$","li",null,{"children":"Physical gathering, once monthly"}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":"2 hours total (we'll treat this as ~90 minutes of actual play after settling in)"}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":"3 players + GM"}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":"No digital tooling assumed (though not prohibited)"}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":"4-6 week gaps between sessions as baseline, occasionally longer"}],"\n"]}]
b5:["$","p",null,{"children":["$","strong",null,{"children":"Scope constraints?"}]}]
b6:["$","p",null,{"children":"The GM needs something they can run, not something they need to design from scratch. This pushes toward existing systems or light modifications rather than ground-up creation. The GM also has limited prep time—they're a busy adult too."}]
b7:["$","p",null,{"children":["$","strong",null,{"children":"Setting?"}]}]
b8:["$","p",null,{"children":["$","em",null,{"children":"Framework asks: Does setting need to be load-bearing or can it be cosmetic?"}]}]
b9:["$","p",null,{"children":"The players want fantasy—it's what they know from D&D, it satisfies nostalgia, and it has vocabulary they already understand. But nothing in their core needs requires fantasy mechanically. The problems they're experiencing (memory, rules overhead, session incompleteness) are structural, not setting-dependent."}]
ba:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Our answer:"}]," Fantasy setting, cosmetic (Level 1-2 on Space Coffee scale). We're leveraging their existing genre knowledge to reduce cognitive load. We could reskin to any setting without changing the core design. This is a feature—if one player really wants space opera instead, the system should accommodate that."]}]

bc:["$","p",null,{"children":"This is where the framework forces clarity that might otherwise be missed."}]
bd:["$","p",null,{"children":["$","em",null,{"children":"Framework notes: The players say \"D&D\" but D&D is actually multiple archetypes awkwardly combined:"}]}]
be:["$","ul",null,{"children":["\n",["$","li",null,{"children":"Tactical combat (the combat system with its action economy and grid positioning)"}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":"Dungeon crawl (the original exploration and resource-management structure)"}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":"Heroic adventure (the power fantasy and narrative arc)"}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":"Campaign progression (character advancement over extended play)"}],"\n"]}]
bf:["$","p",null,{"children":["$","em",null,{"children":"Which are they actually asking for?"}]}]
c0:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"GM's answer:"}]," \"They loved combat. Or at least they remember loving it. They definitely want to feel like heroes fighting monsters. But the combats we ran last time took forever—one fight was most of a session, and then we had to stop mid-dungeon.\""]}]
c1:["$","p",null,{"children":"So they want combat. But D&D-style tactical combat takes 30-60 minutes per encounter. In a 2-hour session, that's one or two fights maximum, with no room for anything else. The archetype as D&D implements it is temporally incompatible with their constraints."}]
c2:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"The framework helps us see a crucial distinction:"}]," They want the ",["$","em",null,{"children":"fantasy"}]," of tactical combat (heroes fighting monsters, using cool abilities, working together) but they cannot afford the ",["$","em",null,{"children":"implementation"}]," of tactical combat (grid positioning, action economy, modifier calculation, multi-round attrition)."]}]
c3:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Our archetype answer:"}]," Heroic Adventure with Fast Combat."]}]
c4:["$","p",null,{"children":"This means:"}]
c5:["$","ul",null,{"children":["\n",["$","li",null,{"children":"Combat exists and matters"}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":"Combat is light, cooperative, decisive"}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":"Combat resolves in minutes, not half-hours"}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":"The feel is heroic and exciting, not tactical and crunchy"}],"\n"]}]
c6:["$","p",null,{"children":["Additionally: ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"Episodic structure with Campaign persistence."}]]}]
c7:["$","p",null,{"children":"Each session is a complete episode. But episodes connect—characters grow, the world remembers, long-term stories develop. This is TV-season structure, not movie structure or continuous-novel structure."}]

ca:["$","p",null,{"children":["$","strong",null,{"children":"What Context eliminates:"}]}]
cb:["$","ul",null,{"children":["\n",["$","li",null,{"children":"Rules-heavy systems (lookup time is failure mode)"}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":"Grid-based tactical combat (time budget incompatible)"}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":"Complex character builds (memory decay over gaps)"}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":"Continuous narrative without episode boundaries (cliffhangers are failure mode)"}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":"Heavy GM prep (GM is also time-constrained)"}],"\n"]}]

This is why D&D fails for them—not because it's bad, but because it's the wrong tool for their situation. The framework has already prevented us from trying to \"fix D&D\" when we should be selecting the right archetype."]}]

10a:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Collaborative creation"}],": Players build on each other's contributions. 136:["$","p",null,{"children":"Chapter 2 introduced system functions. Let's define what each needs to do for our aesthetics:"}]
137:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Adjudication:"}]," Fast, clear, dramatic. No calculation time, no ambiguity, results that feel meaningful. This eliminates complex modifier stacking and table lookups."]}]
138:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Information Management:"}]," Aggressive transparency with fiction-based uncertainty. Players always know what their characters can do and what's at stake. Mystery comes from the fiction, not from system opacity."]}]
139:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Content Generation:"}]," GM-light, fiction-forward. Content emerges from player choices, simple prompts, and collaborative establishment—not from extensive GM prep."]}]
13a:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"State Persistence:"}]," Robust memory with minimal tracking. The game must remember who characters are, what they've done, what's happening in the world—but players and GM cannot be expected to hold this in their heads across 6-week gaps. The system must ",["$","em",null,{"children":"externalize memory"}],"."]}]
13b:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Feedback:"}]," Immediate, social, celebratory. Rolls happen in the open, outcomes are narrated instantly, the table reacts together."]}]
13c:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Cognitive Framing:"}]," Fiction-first. Players think in terms of fiction (\"I intimidate the guard\") not mechanics (\"I use my Bold approach to make an Overcome action\")."]}]
13d:["$","h2",null,{"className":"flex scroll-m-28 flex-row items-center gap-2","id":"anti-dynamics-what-we-must-prevent","children":[["$","a",null,{"data-card":"","href":"#anti-dynamics-what-we-must-prevent","className":"peer","children":"Anti-Dynamics (What We Must Prevent)"}],["$","svg",null,{"ref":"$undefined","xmlns":"http://www.w3.org/2000/svg","width":24,"height":24,"viewBox":"0 0 24 24","fill":"none","stroke":"currentColor","strokeWidth":2,"strokeLinecap":"round","strokeLinejoin":"round","className":"lucide size-3.5 shrink-0 text-fd-muted-foreground opacity-0 transition-opacity peer-hover:opacity-100","aria-label":"Link to section","children":[[["$","path","1cjeqo",{"d":"M10 13a5 5 0 0 0 7.54.54l3-3a5 5 0 0 0-7.07-7.07l-1.72 1.71"}],["$","path","19qd67",{"d":"M14 11a5 5 0 0 0-7.54-.54l-3 3a5 5 0 0 0 7.07 7.07l1.71-1.71"}]],"$undefined"]}]]}]
13e:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Prevent: Analysis paralysis"}]," — Long decision-making kills Fellowship (others disengage) and pacing (Narrative stalls). ",["$","em",null,{"children":"Solution:"}]," Limited options, fast resolution, forward momentum."]}]
13f:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Prevent: Rules lawyering"}]," — Arguments about mechanics destroy Fellowship and break immersion. ",["$","em",null,{"children":"Solution:"}]," GM authority clear, rules simple enough to not dispute, fiction-first resolution."]}]

19b:["$","p",null,{"children":"This is the cliffhanger problem. Mid-combat, mid-negotiation, mid-revelation—these stops mean 4-6 weeks of unresolved tension. Players forget the specifics but remember the frustration."}]

1bc:["$","p",null,{"children":"Balance paradigm determines how the game maintains appropriate challenge, fairness, and engagement. The framework offers three paradigms:"}]
1bd:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Consistency Paradigm:"}]," Fixed rules, deterministic outcomes, player skill as variable. The system behaves identically regardless of player state."]}]
1be:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Framework Paradigm:"}]," Rules provide structure and boundaries, but human judgment determines specific outcomes. A GM or group consensus handles what rules cannot specify."]}]
1bf:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Adaptive Paradigm:"}]," System adjusts to player state, maintaining target experience regardless of skill level."]}]
1c0:["$","p",null,{"children":["$","em",null,{"children":"Framework prompts: How is difficulty managed? How much player customization is supported? Who or what makes judgment calls? How does the system handle edge cases?"}]}]
1c1:["$","h2",null,{"className":"flex scroll-m-28 flex-row items-center gap-2","id":"why-framework-paradigm-is-required","children":[["$","a",null,{"data-card":"","href":"#why-framework-paradigm-is-required","className":"peer","children":"Why Framework Paradigm Is Required"}],["$","svg",null,{"ref":"$undefined","xmlns":"http://www.w3.org/2000/svg","width":24,"height":24,"viewBox":"0 0 24 24","fill":"none","stroke":"currentColor","strokeWidth":2,"strokeLinecap":"round","strokeLinejoin":"round","className":"lucide size-3.5 shrink-0 text-fd-muted-foreground opacity-0 transition-opacity peer-hover:opacity-100","aria-label":"Link to section","children":[[["$","path","1cjeqo",{"d":"M10 13a5 5 0 0 0 7.54.54l3-3a5 5 0 0 0-7.07-7.07l-1.72 1.71"}],["$","path","19qd67",{"d":"M14 11a5 5 0 0 0-7.54-.54l-3 3a5 5 0 0 0 7.07 7.07l1.71-1.71"}]],"$undefined"]}]]}]
1c2:["$","p",null,{"children":"Our constraints make this nearly inevitable:"}]
1c3:["$","p",null,{"children":["$","strong",null,{"children":"Time constraint eliminates Consistency:"}]}]
1c4:["$","p",null,{"children":"Consistency paradigm requires comprehensive rules—every situation has a defined resolution. This works for D&D because you can (theoretically) look up grappling rules, falling damage tables, or spell interactions."}]
1c5:["$","p",null,{"children":"But we have 90 minutes and \"rules lookup\" is an explicit failure mode. We cannot have rules comprehensive enough for Consistency paradigm while also having rules simple enough to never require lookup."}]
1c6:["$","p",null,{"children":["$","strong",null,{"children":"Memory constraint eliminates Consistency:"}]}]
1c7:["$","p",null,{"children":"Consistency requires players to know rules. With 4-6 week gaps, players will not retain rule knowledge. Every session would require re-teaching, burning our precious time budget."}]
1c8:["$","p",null,{"children":["$","strong",null,{"children":"Narrative aesthetic requires Framework:"}]}]
1c9:["$","p",null,{"children":"Narrative emerges from judgment calls. \"Does the dragon believe this lie?\" can't be fully determined by rules—it depends on fiction, history, character, plausibility. A GM must judge."}]
1ca:["$","p",null,{"children":["$","strong",null,{"children":"Fellowship aesthetic requires Framework:"}]}]
1cb:["$","p",null,{"children":"Fellowship means reading the room. Is everyone engaged? Is someone hogging spotlight? Is this combat dragging? These require human judgment and adjustment in real-time."}]
1cc:["$","p",null,{"children":["$","strong",null,{"children":"Adaptive paradigm doesn't fit:"}]}]
1cd:["$","p",null,{"children":"Adaptive paradigm (like Left 4 Dead's AI Director) adjusts difficulty algorithmically based on player performance. This requires either digital implementation or mechanical complexity we can't afford. It also feels manipulative when visible in tabletop—players don't want to know the GM is secretly adjusting numbers."}]
1ce:["$","p",null,{"children":["$","strong",null,{"children":"Our answer: Framework Paradigm with GM tools"}]}]
1cf:["$","p",null,{"children":["The GM is the balance mechanism. Rules provide structure—they tell you ",["$","em",null,{"children":"when"}]," to roll and ",["$","em",null,{"children":"what outcomes mean"}],"—but the GM determines difficulty, pacing, and fictional outcomes through judgment."]}]

20a:["$","p",null,{"children":"NPC in 30 seconds: Name, Role (what they do), Want (what they're trying to achieve), Quirk (one memorable trait). No stats unless they're an obstacle."}]

20e:["$","p",null,{"children":"Framework paradigm with robust GM tools means:"}]
20f:["$","p",null,{"children":["$","strong",null,{"children":"Players need:"}]}]
210:["$","ul",null,{"children":["\n",["$","li",null,{"children":"Clear character capabilities (what can I do?)"}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":"Simple resolution understanding (when do I roll? what do results mean?)"}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":"Trust in GM fairness (rulings feel consistent and reasonable)"}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":"Permission to contribute to fiction (collaborative, not GM-dictated)"}],"\n"]}]
211:["$","p",null,{"children":["$","strong",null,{"children":"Players don't need:"}]}]
212:["$","ul",null,{"children":["\n",["$","li",null,{"children":"Deep rules knowledge (GM handles complexity)"}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":"Tactical optimization (GM balances encounters to drama, not math)"}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":"System mastery (fiction-first means fiction knowledge matters more)"}],"\n"]}]
213:["$","p",null,{"children":["$","strong",null,{"children":"The trade-off:"}]}]

276:["$","ol",null,{"children":["\n",["$","li",null,{"children":["\n",["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Frame the fight:"}]," Who's here? What's the environment? 396:["$","p",null,{"children":"We began with a request that could have gone anywhere: \"Help three busy professionals play D&D together.\" Without structure, a designer might have started hacking D&D's encumbrance rules or debating initiative systems. 397:["$","p",null,{"children":"The answer—Heroic Adventure, not Tactical Combat—reframed the entire project. We weren't fixing D&D; we were building something for a different purpose entirely. That insight emerged from Level 0, before any mechanical work began."}]
398:["$","p",null,{"children":"This is what the framework does. It doesn't generate designs automatically. It asks the right questions in the right order, and each answer constrains what comes next."}]

39a:["$","p",null,{"children":"Watch how each level built on the previous:"}]
39b:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Level 0"}]," established that monthly sessions with long gaps required episodic structure and external memory support. This wasn't a preference—it was a constraint."]}]
39c:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Level 1"}]," identified Fellowship and Narrative as primary aesthetics, but flagged a tension: Narrative typically requires engagement that casual schedules can't support. Rather than compromise, we carried this forward as a design challenge."]}]
39d:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Level 2"}]," translated those aesthetics into required dynamics, including \"rapid context reconstruction\"—a dynamic that doesn't exist in most games because most games don't need it."]}]
39e:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Level 3"}]," designed the temporal architecture around that constraint: Previously On, Next Time On, Session Records. The memory problem got solved through structure, not rules."]}]
39f:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Level 4"}]," eliminated most balance paradigms through constraint analysis. Consistency requires comprehensive rules these players can't maintain. Adaptive requires technology that doesn't fit tabletop. Framework was the only viable option—not a preference, a derivation."]}]
3a0:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Level 5"}]," built mechanics that serve the dynamics: fiction-first resolution, Position/Effect for transparent GM judgment, stress that resets between sessions, aspects that externalize character identity onto physical cards."]}]
3a1:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Level 6"}]," specified how everything reaches players: verbal rituals that shift modes, physical artifacts that survive gaps, GM tools that enable Framework balance without overwhelming preparation."]}]
3a2:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Level 7"}]," derived specific numbers from measurable targets: 5 stress boxes because heroes should survive 3-5 hits; 3d6 baseline because 82% success rate feels heroic; 10-15 minute combats because that's what the time budget allows."]}]
3a3:["$","p",null,{"children":"No level was skipped. No level was arbitrary. Each built on what came before."}]

3aa:["$","p",null,{"children":"The framework doesn't hand you answers. It asks questions. When you answer, it asks follow-up questions, points out tensions, and constrains your options. 3ad:["$","p",null,{"children":["One thing this derivation revealed: the framework produces ",["$","em",null,{"children":"designs"}],", not ",["$","em",null,{"children":"documents"}],"."]}]
3ae:["$","p",null,{"children":"At the end of Level 7, we had a complete, validated system specification. We did not have printable character sheets, quick reference cards, a starting adventure, or an example of play. Those production artifacts require additional work—work the framework doesn't address."}]
3af:["$","p",null,{"children":"This isn't a flaw. Design and production are different activities. But designers should understand that completing a derivation is not the same as completing a game. The path from validated design to playable product requires attention to presentation, layout, teaching, and accessibility that the framework treats as downstream concerns."}]
3b0:["$","h2",null,{"className":"flex scroll-m-28 flex-row items-center gap-2","id":"what-makes-this-different","children":[["$","a",null,{"data-card":"","href":"#what-makes-this-different","className":"peer","children":"What Makes This Different"}],["$","svg",null,{"ref":"$undefined","xmlns":"http://www.w3.org/2000/svg","width":24,"height":24,"viewBox":"0 0 24 24","fill":"none","stroke":"currentColor","strokeWidth":2,"strokeLinecap":"round","strokeLinejoin":"round","className":"lucide size-3.5 shrink-0 text-fd-muted-foreground opacity-0 transition-opacity peer-hover:opacity-100","aria-label":"Link to section","children":[[["$","path","1cjeqo",{"d":"M10 13a5 5 0 0 0 7.54.54l3-3a5 5 0 0 0-7.07-7.07l-1.72 1.71"}],["$","path","19qd67",{"d":"M14 11a5 5 0 0 0-7.54-.54l-3 3a5 5 0 0 0 7.07 7.07l1.71-1.71"}]],"$undefined"]}]]}]
3b1:["$","p",null,{"children":"Many design methodologies start with mechanics and hope aesthetics emerge. The framework inverts this: start with what players should feel, derive what dynamics create those feelings, then build mechanics that generate those dynamics."}]
3b2:["$","p",null,{"children":"Many design methodologies treat balance as a tuning problem—playtest and adjust until it feels right. The framework treats balance as an architectural decision made early, with specific consequences for every subsequent choice."}]
3b3:["$","p",null,{"children":"Many design methodologies skip from concept to implementation. The framework insists on temporal architecture—how does this game structure time?—before any mechanical work begins. This prevents a common failure mode: systems that work moment-to-moment but fail session-to-session or campaign-to-campaign."}]

3b7:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"A model for the conversation"}]," between designer and framework. Notice how each level's output becomes the next level's input. Notice how tensions get flagged and carried forward rather than ignored or immediately resolved."]}]
3b8:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"A demonstration of constraint productivity"}],". Every limitation—monthly sessions, casual engagement, long gaps—became a design feature. Constraints aren't problems to overcome; they're parameters that shape solutions."]}]
3b9:["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Evidence that the framework scales"}],". Hearthfire addresses a complex design challenge (Fellowship + Narrative for casual players with episodic schedules) that could easily have produced incoherent compromises. The framework kept everything aligned."]}]
